  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_585d3b0d-0d85-4f8d-a36e-fed83f4db523'
      });

  <span id="freeText1745832198727826755" style="display:none">Keine Zeugen, keine Spuren, keine Leiche. Josy, die zwölfjährige Tochter des bekannten Psychiaters Viktor Larenz, verschwindet unter mysteriösen Umständen. Ihr Schicksal bleibt ungeklärt.<br />Vier Jahre später: Der trauernde Viktor hat sich in ein abgelegenes Ferienhaus zurückgezogen. Doch eine schöne Unbekannte spürt ihn dort auf. Sie wird von Wahnvorstellungen gequält. Darin erscheint ihr immer wieder ein kleines Mädchen, das ebenso spurlos verschwindet wie einst Josy. Viktor beginnt mit der Therapie, die mehr und mehr zum dramatischen Verhör wird...</span>

<div id="review_2736191824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736191824" />
    <a title="Nazanin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39893246-nazanin"><img alt="Nazanin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600407709p2/39893246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736191824?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nazanin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nazanin" href="/user/show/39893246-nazanin">Nazanin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19187015-therapy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39893246-nazanin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39893246-nazanin?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39893246-nazanin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39893246-nazanin?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736191824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5167089130160044422"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>Dr. Viktor Larenz’s twelve-year-old girl, Josy, was ill, had mysterious symptoms and doctors didn’t know what was her illness. One day, he left her in the waiting room of the doc’s office to fetch her some water and when he came back Josy wasn’t there. He thought she went to the doc’s office but she had vanished into the thin air...<br/><br/>Four years later Josy is still missing. A mental patient (suffers from schizophrenia) turned up on his doorstep. She is a novelist for children and she is conv</span>
  <span id="freeText5167089130160044422" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />Dr. Viktor Larenz’s twelve-year-old girl, Josy, was ill, had mysterious symptoms and doctors didn’t know what was her illness. One day, he left her in the waiting room of the doc’s office to fetch her some water and when he came back Josy wasn’t there. He thought she went to the doc’s office but she had vanished into the thin air...<br /><br />Four years later Josy is still missing. A mental patient (suffers from schizophrenia) turned up on his doorstep. She is a novelist for children and she is convinced that she’s being hounded by characters of her books. She is sure each character she writes, they come alive in real life. And one of the stories is so much like Josy’s…<br /><br /><i>Who is she? How does she know about Josy? What’s taking her so long? Can Anna's delusions describe Josy's last days? Where is his daughter?</i><br /><br />Told in mostly single POV, 3rd person. It’s a standalone novel, well-written and fast-paced with short chapters, unreliable characters and with a satisfactory ending. It was a good engaging thriller. It was my first read by this author and it won’t be my last. Overall, I had a good time reading this and hope you enjoy it as well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5167089130160044422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2181345841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2181345841" />
    <a title="Andrew Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith"><img alt="Andrew Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605605555p2/5885760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2181345841?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Smith" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith">Andrew Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19187015-therapy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2181345841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12721957299028403919">I’ve read a few book written by this German author – all translated into English from his mother tongue. Fitzeck seems to specialise in creating scenes of tortuous intrigue and suspense before landing a twisting finish that gives the lie to the readers understanding of events previously described. In this story, we first meet Dr Viktor Larenz, a renowned psychiatrist who is in a state of panic at what he perceives to be the disappearance of his twelve-year-old daughter, Josy. He’d left her in th</span>
  <span id="freeText12721957299028403919" style="display:none">I’ve read a few book written by this German author – all translated into English from his mother tongue. Fitzeck seems to specialise in creating scenes of tortuous intrigue and suspense before landing a twisting finish that gives the lie to the readers understanding of events previously described. In this story, we first meet Dr Viktor Larenz, a renowned psychiatrist who is in a state of panic at what he perceives to be the disappearance of his twelve-year-old daughter, Josy. He’d left her in the offices of another doctor for a few minutes during which time she appears to have been abducted. In the months and years that follow, struggling to deal with this devastating event, Larenz takes to the drink and in time his wife leaves him. His life in tatters, he closes down his professional practice.<br /><br />The scene then shifts to a psychosomatic clinic where Lorenz, under restraint, is talking to a fellow psychiatrist who is trying to dig the back story out of him. Why exactly is he here? And why under restraint? Is Larenz, in fact, accused of killing his own daughter? It’s not clear. In fact, nothing is clear. As the scene continues, we start to hear Larenz’s account of recent events – now, it’s promised, we’ll learn of Josy’s fate.<br /><br />As Larenz starts to speak we hear that some years after Josy’s disappearance he had secreted himself away away on an isolated island. Here he was visited by a young woman, Anna Glass, who persuaded him to hear her story, promising him that he’d want to treat her when he’s heard her out. Reluctant as he is to entertain this intrusion, and adamant that he is that he is no longer a practising doctor, he does eventually find himself hooked by Anna’s story. <br /><br />The whole tale is told in a breathless style somewhat reminiscent of a Dan Brown novel and, in truth, I found this rather overblown and tiresome. But despite this I was intrigued – how was all this going to play out? It’s a pacy psychological thriller with my only real gripe (apart from the hyperbole, that is) being that I found the twists at the end to be at first clever but then veering sharply toward the unbelievable. It’s a pity, as I think a bit more of a risk could have been taken to produce a more memorable climax. <br /><br />It’s an entertaining tale though, and one certainly worth catching if you enjoy tantalising psychological thrillers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12721957299028403919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3506189433465691867" style="display:none">Rating 4* out of 5. I'm trying to figure out how to say something elegant about this book, but I can't. This was a total mindfuck from start to finish. Of course I had my suspicions and I wasn't totally wrong... But yeah, I was. Totally up every wall and down the other side. Every one of my theories was right in the end. That's not supposed to happen! ONE theory is supposed to be right. Not all of them. No one ever ties such a story together. Except Fitzek.<br /><br />Viktor Larenz, famous psychiatrist, lost his 12-year old daughter Josephine four years ago. He is now isolated on an island, licking his wounds. Then a strange woman, Anna, turns up and demands therapy, which quickly turns into an interrogation. Nothing is what it seems. Everyone around Viktor behaves erratically and it is difficult to separate truth from fiction, no pun intended.<br /><br />Read this at your own peril. Don't start it late in the evening, it will keep you up all night.<br /><br />Filed to reading challenge 2015, category "thriller". </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer281825844052667952">My second delve into this author having really enjoyed Splinter, one of his lower rated books!<br/><br/>It begins in a psychiatric hospital with the patient (a former psychologist) & doctor reviewing his case history.... the story is thus retold as he lays strapped to the bed, how he has got their we don’t know at the start, why he can’t be untied again we are not told..... the story begins..... from quite early on you are starting to surmise what is fact & fantasy as all seems slightly outta whack with t</span>
  <span id="freeText281825844052667952" style="display:none">My second delve into this author having really enjoyed Splinter, one of his lower rated books!<br /><br />It begins in a psychiatric hospital with the patient (a former psychologist) &amp; doctor reviewing his case history.... the story is thus retold as he lays strapped to the bed, how he has got their we don’t know at the start, why he can’t be untied again we are not told..... the story begins..... from quite early on you are starting to surmise what is fact &amp; fantasy as all seems slightly outta whack with the Dear Doctor but you are never really sure &amp; I found it a very addictive read which hooked me from page 1 reading into the night.<br /><br />To tell you any more would ruin it!<br /><br />If you’ve never come across the author I highly recommend you try one especially if the physiological mystery genre is your thing. 4 Stars for me &amp; more from this author for sure.<br /></span>

<div id="review_118716933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118716933" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1803230-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278898706p2/1803230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118716933?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/1803230-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/8435267-therapy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118716933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9331304734742116741">Dr. Viktor Larenz is a renowned Psychotherapist, but his life falls apart the day his 12 year old daughter Josy disappears. Fours year later, Viktor is taking a break on the island of Parkum, when a strange woman called Anna Glass insists she needs him to give her therapy sessions. When she starts talking about a character in her book, a young girl that ran away, Viktor wonders if she could possibly be referring to his daughter, and if he might he find out what happened to her after all?<br/><br/>This boo</span>
  <span id="freeText9331304734742116741" style="display:none">Dr. Viktor Larenz is a renowned Psychotherapist, but his life falls apart the day his 12 year old daughter Josy disappears. Fours year later, Viktor is taking a break on the island of Parkum, when a strange woman called Anna Glass insists she needs him to give her therapy sessions. When she starts talking about a character in her book, a young girl that ran away, Viktor wonders if she could possibly be referring to his daughter, and if he might he find out what happened to her after all?<br /><br />This book was quite frankly, one of the best I've read in the psychological thriller genre. The whole thing from start to finish was written to play with your mind, and it does it oh so well too. When you think you've guessed what happened, something else is revealed blowing your theories out of the water. The story is well written, as are the characters, and I was so gripped I found it impossible to put down until I was finished. The ending was a complete surprise, which I didn't see coming at all, and I love those kinds of endings. I cannot recommend this higly enough to fans of this genre. When more of his work is translated, I will be first in the queue!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9331304734742116741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15989132417006642018">At first I thought that I wont be able to finish this book. Short chapters that seemed to be all over the place. Had to re-read parts thinking I had missed something but I hadn't. Then one morning as I was eating breakfast it dawned on me that for the last 15 minutes I had done nothing but think about this book. What the hell was going on in this book. Who were the villains, if there were any, and were there any good guys? Without realising it I had been sucked right in. I now needed, and wanted</span>
  <span id="freeText15989132417006642018" style="display:none">At first I thought that I wont be able to finish this book. Short chapters that seemed to be all over the place. Had to re-read parts thinking I had missed something but I hadn't. Then one morning as I was eating breakfast it dawned on me that for the last 15 minutes I had done nothing but think about this book. What the hell was going on in this book. Who were the villains, if there were any, and were there any good guys? Without realising it I had been sucked right in. I now needed, and wanted, to know what was going on. The end came as a surprise and was nothing like I expected. Can't say it was a great read but for all that I enjoyed it and wouldn't hesitate to recommend it. The first Fitzek book I read was (Splinter) and that really was a great read. I will be reading more of his works in the future.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13624585677697554744">A real page-turner. If you are familiar with some of Fitzek's works, the themes of this book won't be that unfamiliar to you and perhaps you won't even be surprised when the twist is revealed. But beware, with Fitzek there's always another, bigger, more unpredictable twist and that is precisely what puts his books on the top of the list for mystery and thriller fans. I thoroughly enjoyed this one, as evident from the fact that i finished it in a day.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917110292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13489945643873434476">I have to say, I didn’t see that coming. I feel like the less you know about the book, the more you’ll enjoy it. It reads really fast, and even though you can tell something is odd, you are still surprised. At least I was. I had some problems with the writing, but that was it. Also, this is his first book, so I took that in consideration. I will reread it, because I want to see if I can find some details I missed this time. I recommend it if you want a good mystery that you can read in a day. It</span>
  <span id="freeText13489945643873434476" style="display:none">I have to say, I didn’t see that coming. I feel like the less you know about the book, the more you’ll enjoy it. It reads really fast, and even though you can tell something is odd, you are still surprised. At least I was. I had some problems with the writing, but that was it. Also, this is his first book, so I took that in consideration. I will reread it, because I want to see if I can find some details I missed this time. I recommend it if you want a good mystery that you can read in a day. It made me want to check more books about the author!<br /><br />Tengo que decir, no me lo esperaba. Me parece que mientras menos se sepa del libro, más se disfruta. Se lee muy rápido, y aunque te das cuenta que hay algo raro, igual te sorprendés. Por lo menos a mí me pasó. Tuve algunos problemas con la escritura, pero fue lo único. Es su primer libro, así que tuve eso en mente. Lo voy a releer, porque quiero ver si puedo encontrar detalles que se me hayan pasado. Lo recomiendo si quieren un buen misterio que se puede leer en un día. ¡Y voy a leer más del autor!<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aUt+u3rvc15pPf4aFwMA6ZVwIdCiDQk/NDmVj+AAYNoth+7AZSSbrnI24+ZYjVi81M113lNKROA9++8q+s1dIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Дана е сираче, нејзиниот татко дрвосечач загинува во шумска незгода, а од преголема љубов кон него и тага за неговата смрт, по само еден месец умира и нејзината мајка. Па така од нејзиното прекрасно семејство полно со љубов, останува само малата Дана, со вечно скршено срце. Грижата за неа ја презема семејството на братот на татко ѝ, но чичко ѝ и стрина ѝ си имаат свои три деца, свои грижи за гледање, па повеќе ја третираат како слугинка дома и само гледаат да приграбат сè што можат од наследството што ѝ е останато. Дана е прекрасен лик; кротка, мила, послушна, покорна, вредна и пргава – таа не зуцнува дури ни кога тие практично ја продаваат на еден богат пар во Скопје, за да им биде домашна помошничка. Ги голта солзите во себе, а однадвор и понатаму останува силна и истрајна.\n\n„Ќерката на дрвосечачот“ е книга која раскажува за мајчинската љубов, за женската издржливост, за човечката злоба, за <span id="freeTextContainer2635156958136987512">Sebastian Fitzek was born in Berlin in 1971. After going to law school and being promoted to LL.D., he decided against a juridical profession for a creative occupation in the media. After the traineeship at a private radio station he switched to the competition as head of entertainment and became chief editor later on, thereafter becoming an independent executive consultant and format developer fo</span>
  <span id="freeText2635156958136987512" style="display:none">Sebastian Fitzek was born in Berlin in 1971. After going to law school and being promoted to LL.D., he decided against a juridical profession for a creative occupation in the media. After the traineeship at a private radio station he switched to the competition as head of entertainment and became chief editor later on, thereafter becoming an independent executive consultant and format developer for numerous media companies in Europe. He lives in Berlin and is currently working in the programme management of a major capital radio station. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2635156958136987512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
